Curators can set up descriptors for the type of games they are interested in, preferred languages, and other tags along with social media profiles, while developers can find and reach out to specific curators from this information, and, after review, provide them directly with access to their game. This step, which eliminates the use of a Steam redemption key, is aimed at reducing the reselling of keys, as well as dissuading users who may be trying to game the curator system to obtain free game keys.[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-255)

Valve has attempted to deal with "fake games", those that are built around reused assets and little other innovation, by adding Steam Explorers atop its existing Steam Curator program. Any Steam user can sign up to be an Explorer and be asked to look at under-performing games on the service to either vouch that the game is truly original or if it is an example of a "fake game", at which point Valve can take action to remove the game.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-256)[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-257)

In July 2019, the Steam Labs feature was introduced as a means to showcase experimental discovery features Valve considered for including into Steam, to seek public feedback. For example, an initial experiment released at launch was the Interactive Recommender, which uses [artificial intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence") algorithms pulling data from the user's past gameplay history to suggest new games that may be of interest to them.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-258) As these experiments mature through end-user testing, they have then been brought into the storefront as direct features.[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-259)

The September 2019 Discovery update, which Valve claimed would improve the visibility of niche and lesser-known games, was met with criticism from some indie game developers, who recorded a significant drop in the exposure of their games, including new wishlist additions and appearances in the "More Like This" and "Discovery queue" sections of the store.[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-260)[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-261)

Steam Charts were introduced in September 2022 and publicly track the storefront's best-selling and most-played games, including historically by week and month. Charts replaced a previous statistics page to be more comprehensive, and features content that had previously been part of third-party websites including [SteamSpy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SteamSpy "SteamSpy"), SteamDB, and SteamCharts.[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-262)

Games and account policies
--------------------------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: Games and account policies")]

In June 2015, Valve created a formal process to allow purchasers to request refunds, with refunds guaranteed within the first two weeks as long as the player had not spent more than two hours in a game.[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-263) Prior to June 2015, Valve had a no-refunds policy, but allowed them in certain circumstances, such as digital rights management issues or false advertising.[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-264)[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-265)[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-266)

Games that are no longer available for sale for various reasons can still be downloaded and played by those who have already purchased these.[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-cinemablend_gtavc-267)

### Quality control and disallowed functionality

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Quality control and disallowed functionality")]

With the launch of Steam Direct, effectively removing any curation of games by Valve prior to being published on Steam, there have been several incidents of published games that have attempted to mislead Steam users. Starting in June 2018, Valve has taken actions against games and developers that are "[trolling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trolling "Trolling")" the system; in September 2018, Valve explicitly defined that trolls on Steam "aren't actually interested in [good faith](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_faith "Good faith") efforts to make and sell games to you or anyone".[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-jun2018_valve_policy-268)[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-pcgamer_sept2018_policy-269) As an example, Valve's Lombardi stated that the game _[Active Shooter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Active\_Shooter "Active Shooter")_, which would have allowed the player to play as either a SWAT team member tasked to take down the shooter at a school shooting incident or as the shooter themselves, was an example of trolling, as he described it was "designed to do nothing but generate outrage and cause conflict through its existence".[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-vb_trolling-270) Within a month of clarifying its definition of trolling, Valve removed approximately 170 games from Steam.[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-271)

In addition to removing bad actors, Valve has also taken steps to reduce the impact of "fake games" which could be used to manipulate the trading card marketplace or artificially boost a user's Steam level, in addition to changes in Steam to prevent such abuse.[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-272)[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-273)[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-274) Some of these changes have resulted in select [false positives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/False_positive "False positive") for legitimate games with unusual end-user usage patterns, such as _[Wandersong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wandersong "Wandersong")_ which was flagged in January 2019 for what the developer believed was related to near-unanimous positive user reviews from the game.[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-275)

Other actions taken by developers against the terms of service or other policies have prompted Valve to remove games,[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-276) which has included [asset flips](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asset_flip "Asset flip"),[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-277) review manipulation,[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-278) misuse of Steamworks tools,[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-279)[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-280)[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-281) and hostile activities towards Steam users.[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-282)

Valve has banned games that incorporate [blockchain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blockchain "Blockchain")-type technologies, such as [non-fungible tokens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-fungible_token "Non-fungible token") (NFTs) since 2022 due to the questionable nature of their markets.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-283) With the rise of [generative artificial intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generative_artificial_intelligence "Generative artificial intelligence") in 2023, Valve originally established that games with content generated in this manner could be distributed through Steam, though cautioned developers about assuring that they had the rights for this type of content.[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-284) As greater concerns about the copyright and ethical nature of generational AI in the latter half of 2023, Valve clarified its stance in January 2024, requiring games that did use content from generational AI to disclose this on the game's store page, including methods that the developers used to assure the AI engines did not generate illegal content.[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-285) Valve updated policies in February to ban games that incorporated paid advertising as part of the gameplay cycle, such as viewing an ad for virtual rewards.[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-286)

### Mature content and moderation

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Mature content and moderation")]

Valve has also removed or threatened to remove games due to inappropriate or mature content, though there was often confusion as to what material qualified for this. For example, Eek Games' _[House Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House\_Party\_(video\_game) "House Party (video game)")_ included scenes of nudity and sexual encounters in its original release, which drew criticism from conservative religious organization [National Center on Sexual Exploitation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Center_on_Sexual_Exploitation "National Center on Sexual Exploitation"), leading Valve to remove the title. Eek Games later included censor bars within the game, allowing the game to be added back to Steam, though they offered a patch on their website to remove the bars.[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-287) In May 2018, several developers of anime-stylized games that contained some light nudity, such as _[HuniePop](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HuniePop "HuniePop")_, were told by Valve they had to address sexual content within their games or face removal from Steam, leading to questions of inconsistent application of Valve's policies. The National Center on Sexual Exploitation took credit for convincing Valve to target these games. However, Valve later rescinded its orders, allowing these games to remain.[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-288)

In June 2018, Valve clarified its policy on content, taking a more hands-off approach outside of illegal material. Rather than trying to make decisions themselves on what content is appropriate, Valve enhanced its filtering system to allow developers and publishers to indicate and justify the types of mature content (violence, nudity, and sexual content) in their games. Users can block games that are marked with this type of content from appearing in the store, and if they have not blocked it, they are presented with the description before they can continue to the store page. Developers and publishers with existing games on Steam have been strongly encouraged to complete these forms for these games, while Valve will use moderators to make sure new games are appropriately marked.[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-pcgamer_sept2018_policy-269) Valve also committed to developing anti-harassment tools to support developers who may find their game amid controversy.[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-jun2018_valve_policy-268)

> "So we ended up going back to one of the principles in the forefront of our minds when we started Steam, and more recently as we worked on Steam Direct to open up the Store to many more developers: Valve shouldn't be the ones deciding this. If you're a player, we shouldn't be choosing for you what content you can or can't buy. If you're a developer, we shouldn't be choosing what content you're allowed to create. Those choices should be yours to make. Our role should be to provide systems and tools to support your efforts to make these choices for yourself, and to help you do it in a way that makes you feel comfortable."

— Erik Johnson of Valve[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-289)

Until these tools were in place, some adult-themed games were delayed for release.[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-290)[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-291)[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-292)_Negligee: Love Stories_ developed by Dharker Studios was one of the first sexually explicit games to be offered after the introduction of the tools in September 2018. Dharker noted in discussions with Valve that they would be liable for any content-related fines or penalties that countries may place on Valve, a clause of their publishing contract for Steam, and took steps to restrict sale of the game in over 20 regions.[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-293) Games that feature mature themes with primary characters that visually appear to be underaged, even if the game's narrative establishes them as adults, have been banned by Valve.[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-294)

In March 2019, Valve faced pressure over _[Rape Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rape\_Day "Rape Day")_, a planned game described as being a [dark comedy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dark_comedy "Dark comedy") and power fantasy where the player would control a serial rapist amid a zombie apocalypse. Valve ultimately decided against offering the game on Steam, arguing that while it "[respects] developers' desire to express themselves", there were "costs and risks" associated with the game, and the developers had "chosen content matter and a way of representing it that makes it very difficult for us to help them [find an audience]".[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-295)[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-296)

In December 2020, following a complaint from Medienanstalt Hamburg/Schleswig-Holstein regarding store page images on Steam; Valve in Germany opted to block access to games with "Adults Only 18+" pornographic content.[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-297) The [Anti-Defamation League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League "Anti-Defamation League") published a report in November 2024 accusing Valve of allowing the proliferation of hate and anti-semitic content generated by users and user groups, with over 40,000 groups identified to have names referring to such extreme views. Senator [Mark Warner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Warner "Mark Warner") followed with a letter to Valve, asking the company if they were following their published online content policies and to review the cases identified by the ADL.[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-298)

Valve updated its storefront policies in July 2025 to disallow games that "content that may violate the rules and standards set forth by Steam's payment processors and related card networks and banks, or internet network providers", leading to around 400 games rated for mature audiences being pulled from the service. Valve affirmed this change was made due to pressure from banks and payment processors.[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-299)[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-300) This action appeared to arise from an open letter sent to the payment processors by [Collective Shout](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collective_Shout "Collective Shout"), an Australian non-profit group. [Melinda Tankard Reist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melinda_Tankard_Reist "Melinda Tankard Reist"), the leader of Collective Shout, said that they had identified over 500 games with such themes, such as rape, incest and child abuse, leading to the call for payment processors to take action.[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-301) In related actions by September 2025, Valve changed its rules for adult games, disallowing them to use the early access program as part of their game's release,[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-302) and requiring existing games that intend to add mature content to issue that as DLC that can be reviewed by Valve, rather than as a patch.[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-303)

In August 2025, in compliance with the United Kingdom's [Online Safety Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Online_Safety_Act_2023 "Online Safety Act 2023"), Steam began requiring age verification before allowing UK users to view store pages for games with adult content.[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-304) As of September 2025, the only available method of verification is via users adding a valid credit card to their account, which has drawn some criticism surrounding adult users who cannot obtain a credit card.[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-305)

Platforms, devices and regions
------------------------------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Platforms, devices and regions")]

Valve introduced the Steam Hardware Survey in 2003 ahead of the release of _Half-Life 2_. At that time, no information was available as to the distribution of CPU and GPU units among gamers, so Valve used the survey, which automatically collected hardware information with the user's permission through the Steam client, to collect this information and refine the hardware targets for _Half-Life 2_ to meet the widest possible specifications. Since then, Valve continues to use the Steam Hardware Survey to collect hardware distribution information, sharing the net results with other developers to understand the current market, as well as to make choices on when to discontinue support for older hardware and software.[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-306)

### Windows

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Windows")]

Steam was originally released exclusively for [Microsoft Windows](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft_Windows "Microsoft Windows") in 2003, but has since been ported to other platforms.[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-steam_mac-307) More recent Steam client versions use the [Chromium Embedded Framework](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromium_Embedded_Framework "Chromium Embedded Framework").[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-308) To take advantage of some of its features for newer interface elements, Steam uses [64-bit versions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/64-bit_computing "64-bit computing") of Chromium, which makes it unsupported on older operating systems such as [Windows XP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Windows_XP "Windows XP") and [Windows Vista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Windows_Vista "Windows Vista"). Steam on Windows also relies on some security features built into later versions of Windows. Support for XP and Vista was dropped in 2019. While users still on those operating systems can use the client, they do not have access to newer features. Around 0.2% of Steam users were affected by this when it began.[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-309) In March 2023, Valve announced that Steam would drop support for [Windows 7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Windows_7 "Windows 7") and [8](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Windows_8 "Windows 8") on January 1, 2024.[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-310)

### macOS

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: macOS")]

Valve announced a client for [macOS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacOS "MacOS") in March 2010.[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-steam_mac-307) The announcement was preceded by a change in the Steam beta client to support the cross-platform [WebKit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WebKit "WebKit") web browser rendering engine instead of the [Trident engine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trident_(layout_engine) "Trident (layout engine)") of [Internet Explorer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_Explorer "Internet Explorer").[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-311)[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-312)[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-313) Valve teased the release by emailing several images to Mac community and gaming websites; the images featured characters from Valve games with [Apple](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Inc. "Apple Inc.") logos and parodies of vintage [Macintosh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macintosh "Macintosh") advertisements.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-314)[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-CNET_2010_v779-315) Valve developed a full video homage to Apple's _[1984](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1984\_(commercial) "1984 (commercial)")_ Macintosh commercial to announce the availability of _Half-Life 2_ on the service; some concept images for the video had previously been used to tease the Mac Steam client.[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-316)

Steam for macOS was originally planned for release in April 2010 before being pushed back to May 12, 2010. In addition to the Steam client, several features were made available to developers, allowing them to take advantage of the cross-platform Source engine and Steamworks' platform and network capabilities.[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-317) Through the Steam Play functionality, the macOS client allows players who have purchased compatible products in the Windows version to download the Mac versions at no cost.[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-shacknews_mac_release-318) The Steam Cloud, along with many multiplayer PC games, also supports [cross-platform play](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cross-platform_play "Cross-platform play").[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-steam_mac-307)

With Apple discontinuing support for Intel-based Macs after the release of [macOS Tahoe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacOS_Tahoe "MacOS Tahoe") in late 2025 in favor of [Apple silicon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_silicon "Apple silicon"),[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-319) Valve updated the beta version of the Steam client to include native support for Apple silicon without the need for emulation via [Rosetta 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rosetta_(software) "Rosetta (software)").[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-320)

### Linux

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Linux")]

In July 2012, Valve announced that it was developing a client for Linux based on the [Ubuntu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ubuntu "Ubuntu") distribution.[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-linux_announcement-321) This announcement followed months of speculation, primarily from the website [Phoronix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phoronix "Phoronix") that had discovered evidence of Linux developing in recent builds of Steam and other Valve games.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-322) Newell stated that getting Steam and games to work on Linux is a key strategy for Valve; Newell called the closed nature of [Microsoft Windows 8](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft_Windows_8 "Microsoft Windows 8") "a catastrophe for everyone in the PC space", and that Linux would maintain "the openness of the platform".[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-cvg_newell_linux-323) Valve is extending support to any developers that want to bring their games to Linux, by "making it as easy as possible for anybody who's engaged with us—putting their games on Steam and getting those running on Linux", according to Newell.[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-cvg_newell_linux-323)

The team developing the Linux client had been working for a year before the announcement to validate that such a port would be possible.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-gamasutra_linux-324) As of the official announcement, a near-feature-complete Steam client for Linux had been developed and successfully run on Ubuntu.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-gamasutra_linux-324) Internal [beta testing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beta_test "Beta test") of the Linux client started in October 2012; external beta testing occurred in early November the same year.[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-325)[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-326) Open beta clients for Linux were made available in late December 2012,[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-327) and the client was officially released in mid-February 2013.[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-328) At the time of announcement, Valve's Linux division assured that its first game on the OS, _[Left 4 Dead 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Left\_4\_Dead\_2 "Left 4 Dead 2")_, would run at an acceptable frame rate and with a degree of connectivity with the Windows and Mac OS X versions. From there, it began working on porting other games to Ubuntu and expanding to other Linux distributions.[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-linux_announcement-321)[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-329)[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-330) Versions of Steam working under [Fedora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fedora_(operating_system) "Fedora (operating system)") and [Red Hat Enterprise Linux](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Hat_Enterprise_Linux "Red Hat Enterprise Linux") were released by October 2013.[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-331) There were over 500 Linux-compatible games on Steam in June 2014,[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-500LinuxGames-332) and in February 2019, Steam for Linux had 5,800 native games and was described as having "the power to keep Linux [gaming] alive" by [Engadget](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Engadget "Engadget").[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-333)

In August 2018, Valve released a beta version of [Proton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proton_(compatibility_layer) "Proton (compatibility layer)") (named _Steam Play_), an open-source Windows compatibility layer for Linux, so that Linux users could run Windows games on Linux directly through Steam. Proton comprises a set of open-source tools including [Wine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wine_(software) "Wine (software)") and [DXVK](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DXVK "DXVK"). The software allows the use of Steam-supported controllers, even those not compatible with Windows.[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-334) Released in February 2022, Valve's handheld computer, the [Steam Deck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_Deck "Steam Deck"), runs SteamOS 3.0, which is based on [Arch Linux](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arch_Linux "Arch Linux"), and uses Proton to support Windows-based games without native Linux ports.[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-335) Prior to the Steam Deck's release, Valve worked with various middleware developers to make sure their tools were compatible with Proton on Linux and maximize the number of games that the Steam Deck would support. This included working with various anti-cheat developers such as Easy Anti-Cheat and [BattlEye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BattlEye "BattlEye") to make sure their solutions worked with Proton.[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-336)[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-337) To help with compatibility, Valve developed a classification system to rank games based on how well they performed on Steam Deck out of the box.[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-Archer-338)

Support for [Nvidia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nvidia "Nvidia")'s proprietary [deep learning super sampling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_learning_super_sampling "Deep learning super sampling") (DLSS) on supported video cards and games was added to Proton in June 2021, though this is not available on the Steam Deck which is based on AMD hardware.[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-339)[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-340)

In March 2022, Google offered a prerelease version of Steam on [Chromebooks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromebook "Chromebook"),[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-341) and entered public beta in November 2022.[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-342) In August 2025, Google announced that they will end Steam for Chromebook support in 2026.[[342]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-343)

### Steamworks on PlayStation 3

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Steamworks on PlayStation 3")]

At [E3 2010](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/E3_2010 "E3 2010"), Newell announced that Steamworks would arrive on the [PlayStation 3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PlayStation_3 "PlayStation 3") with _Portal 2_.[[343]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-Gamespot_E3_Portal_2-344) Steamworks made its debut on [consoles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_game_console "Video game console") with _Portal 2_'s PlayStation 3 release. Several features—including cross-platform play and [instant messaging](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instant_messaging "Instant messaging"), Steam Cloud for saved games, and the ability for PS3 owners to download _Portal 2_ from Steam (Windows and Mac)—were offered.[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-eurogamer11-ps3-345) Valve's _[Counter-Strike: Global Offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counter-Strike:\_Global\_Offensive "Counter-Strike: Global Offensive")_ also supports Steamworks and cross-platform features on the PlayStation 3, including using keyboard and mouse controls as an alternative to the gamepad.[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-346) Valve said it "hope[s] to expand upon this foundation with more Steam features and functionality in DLC and future content releases".[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-pcgamer-347)

Newell said that they would have liked to bring the service to the Xbox 360 through the game _Counter-Strike: Global Offensive_,[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-348) but later said that cross-platform play would not be present in the final version of the game.[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-349) Valve attributes the inability to use Steamworks on the Xbox 360 to limitations in the Xbox Live regulations of the ability to deliver patches and new content. Valve's Erik Johnson stated that Microsoft required new content on the console to be certified and validated before distribution, which would limit the usefulness of Steamworks' delivery approach.[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-350)

### Mobile apps

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Mobile apps")]

Valve released an official Steam client for [iOS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IOS "IOS") and [Android](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Android_(operating_system) "Android (operating system)") devices in late January 2012, following a short beta period.[[350]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-351) The application allows players to log into their accounts to browse the storefront, manage their games, and communicate with friends in the Steam community. The application also incorporates a [two-factor authentication](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Two-factor_authentication "Two-factor authentication") system that works with Steam Guard. Newell stated that the application was a strong request from Steam users and sees it as a means "to make [Steam] richer and more accessible for everyone".[[351]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-352) A mobile Steam client for [Windows Phone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Windows_Phone "Windows Phone") devices was released in June 2016.[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-353) In May 2019, a mobile chat-only client for Steam was released under the name Steam Chat.[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-354)

On May 14, 2018, a "Steam Link" app with remote play features was released in beta to allow users to stream games to Android phones, named after discontinued set-top box [Steam Link](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_Link "Steam Link").[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-slink_mobile-355) It was also submitted to the [iOS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IOS "IOS")[App Store](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/App_Store_(iOS) "App Store (iOS)"), but was denied by [Apple Inc.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Inc. "Apple Inc."), who cited "business conflicts with app guidelines".[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-slink_mobile-355)[[355]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-356) Apple later clarified its rule at the following [Apple Worldwide Developers Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Worldwide_Developers_Conference "Apple Worldwide Developers Conference") in early June, in that iOS apps may not offer an app-like purchasing store, but does not restrict apps that provide [remote desktop support](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Remote_desktop_software "Remote desktop software").[[356]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-357) In response, Valve removed the ability to purchase games or other content through the app and resubmitted it for approval in June 2018, where it was accepted by Apple and allowed on their store in May 2019.[[357]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-358)[[358]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-359)

### Steam-branded devices

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Steam-branded devices")]

Before 2013, industry analysts believed that Valve was developing hardware and tuning features of Steam with apparent use on its own hardware. These computers were pre-emptively dubbed as "Steam Boxes" by the gaming community and expected to be a dedicated machine focused on Steam functionality and maintaining the core functionality of a traditional video game console.[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-360) In September 2013, Valve unveiled [SteamOS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SteamOS "SteamOS"), a custom [Linux](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linux "Linux")-based operating system they had developed specifically aimed for running Steam and games, and the final concept of the [Steam Machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_Machine_(hardware_platform) "Steam Machine (hardware platform)") hardware.[[360]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-SteamOS-361) Unlike other consoles, the Steam Machine does not have set hardware; its technology is implemented at the discretion of the manufacturer and is fully customizable, much like a personal computer.[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-362) In 2018, the Steam Machines were removed from the storefront due to low sales and small user traffic.[[362]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-363)

In November 2015, Valve released the [set-top box](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Set-top_box "Set-top box")[Steam Link](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_Link "Steam Link") and [Steam Controller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_Controller "Steam Controller") (which was discontinued in 2019).[[363]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-364) The Steam Link removed the need for HDMI cables for displaying a PC's screen and allowed for wireless connection when connecting to a [TV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TV_set "TV set"). That was discontinued in 2018, but now "Steam Link" refers to the Remote Play mobile app that allows users to stream content, such as games, from a PC to a mobile device over a network.[[364]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-365)[[365]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-366)[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-367)

[![Image 8](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Steam_Deck_%28front%29.png/250px-Steam_Deck_%28front%29.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Steam_Deck_(front).png)

Steam Deck

Valve released the [Steam Deck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_Deck "Steam Deck"), a handheld gaming computer running an updated version of [SteamOS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SteamOS "SteamOS"), with initial shipments starting on February 25, 2022.[[367]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-368) The Deck is designed for the play of Steam games, but it can be placed into a separate dock that allows the Deck to output to an external [display](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Display_device "Display device").[[368]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-369) The Deck was released on February 25, 2022.[[369]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-370) Among updates to Steam and SteamOS included better Proton layer support for Windows-based games, improved user interface features in the Steam client for the Steam Deck display, and adding Dynamic Cloud Saves to Steam to allow synchronizing saved games while a game is being played.[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-Mackovich-40) Valve began marking all games on the service through a Steam Deck Validated program to indicate how compatible they were with the Steam Deck software.[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-Archer-338)

### Steam Cloud Play

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Steam Cloud Play")]

Valve included beta support for Steam Cloud Play in May 2020 for developers to allow users to play games in their library which developers and publishers have opted to allow in a [cloud gaming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloud_gaming "Cloud gaming") service. At launch, Steam Cloud Play only worked through Nvidia's [GeForce Now](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GeForce_Now "GeForce Now") service and would link up to other cloud services in the future though whether Valve would run its own cloud gaming service was unclear.[[370]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-371)

### Steam China

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Steam China")]

[![Image 9](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Steam_China_Release_Key_Note_Speech_%28Perfect_World_CEO_Robert_Hong_Xiao%29_01.jpg/250px-Steam_China_Release_Key_Note_Speech_%28Perfect_World_CEO_Robert_Hong_Xiao%29_01.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Steam_China_Release_Key_Note_Speech_(Perfect_World_CEO_Robert_Hong_Xiao)_01.jpg)

The Steam China launch event in August 2019 in Shanghai

[![Image 10](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Steam_China_Release_Event.jpg/250px-Steam_China_Release_Event.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Steam_China_Release_Event.jpg)

Steam China Release Event (featuring [Wallpaper Engine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wallpaper_Engine "Wallpaper Engine"))

China has [strict regulations on video games and Internet use](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_gaming_in_China "Video gaming in China"); however, access to Steam is allowed through China's governmental firewalls. Currently, a large portion of Steam users are from China. By November 2017, more than half of the Steam userbase was fluent in Chinese, an effect created by the large popularity of _[Dota 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dota\_2 "Dota 2")_ and _[PlayerUnknown's Battlegrounds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PlayerUnknown%27s\_Battlegrounds "PlayerUnknown's Battlegrounds")_ in the country,[[371]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-30mChina-372)[[372]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-polygon_china_effect-373) and several developers have reported that Chinese players make up close to 30% of the total players for their games.[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-eg_steam_china-374)

Following a Chinese government-ordered temporary block of many of Steam's functions in December 2017,[[374]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-375) Valve and [Perfect World](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perfect_World_(company) "Perfect World (company)") announced they would help to provide an officially sanctioned version of Steam that meets Chinese Internet requirements. Perfect World has worked with Valve before to help bring _Dota 2_ and _Counter-Strike: Global Offensive_ to the country through approved government processes.[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-eg_steam_china-374)[[375]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-376) All games to be released on Steam China are expected to pass through the government approval process and meet other governmental requirements, such as requiring a Chinese company to run any game with an online presence.[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-eg_steam_china-374)

The platform is known locally as "Steam Platform" ([Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters "Simplified Chinese characters"): 蒸汽平台; [pinyin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinyin "Pinyin"): _Zhēngqì píngtái_) and runs independently from the rest of Steam. It was made to comply with [China's strict regulations on video games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_gaming_in_China "Video gaming in China").[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-377) Valve does not plan to prevent Chinese users from accessing the global Steam platform and will try to assure that a player's cloud data remains usable between the two.[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-eg_steam_china-374) The client launched as an open beta on February 9, 2021, with about 40 games available at launch.[[377]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-378) As of December 2021, only around 100 games that have been reviewed and licensed by the government are available through Steam China.[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-:0-379)

On December 25, 2021, reports emerged that Steam's global service was the target of a domain name system attack that prevented users in China from accessing its site. The Chinese government [Ministry of Industry and Information Technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Industry_and_Information_Technology "Ministry of Industry and Information Technology") (MIIT) later confirmed that Chinese gamers would no longer be able to use Steam's global service as its international domain name has been designated as "illegal". The block has effectively locked all Chinese users out of games they had purchased through Steam's international service.[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-:0-379)[[379]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-380) In 2023, reports emerged that the Steam Store could be used as normal in China, while the Steam Community was still blocked.[[380]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-381)

Reception and impact
--------------------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Reception and impact")]

Steam's success has led to some criticism because it supported DRM and for being an effective monopoly.[[381]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-382)[[382]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-383) In 2012, [Free Software Foundation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation "Free Software Foundation") founder [Richard Stallman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Stallman "Richard Stallman") called DRM using Steam on Linux "unethical", but still better than Windows.[[383]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-384)

Steam's customer service has been highly criticized, with users citing poor response times or lack of response. In March 2015, Valve was given a failing "F" grade from the [Better Business Bureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Better_Business_Bureau "Better Business Bureau") due to a large number of complaints about Valve's handling of Steam, leading Valve's Erik Johnson to state that "we don't feel like our customer service support is where it needs to be right now".[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-bbb-385) Johnson stated the company plans to better integrate customer support features into the Steam client and be more responsive.[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-bbb-385) In May 2017, in addition to hiring more staff for customer service, Valve publicized pages that show the number and type of customer service requests it was handling over the last 90 days, with an average of 75,000 entered each day. Of those, requests for refunds were the largest segment, and which Valve could resolve within hours, followed by account security and recovery requests. Valve stated at this time that 98% of all service requests were processed within 24 hours of filing.[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-386)

### Users and revenue

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Users and revenue")]

In August 2011, Valve said Steam's revenue, estimated to be $1 billion in 2010, was comparable to that of its published games. Gabe Newell said the company was "tremendously profitable", being more profitable per employee than companies like [Google](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google "Google") or [Apple](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Inc. "Apple Inc.").[[386]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-387) Valve reported that there were 125 million active accounts on Steam by the end of 2015.[[b]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-389) By August 2017, the company reported that there were 27 million new active accounts since January 2016, bringing the total number of active users to at least 150 million.[[388]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-geekwire_aug2017-390) Most accounts were from North America and Western Europe, with there being a significant growth in accounts from Asia around 2017, spurred by their work to help localize the client and make additional currency options available to purchasers.[[388]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-geekwire_aug2017-390) In September 2014, 1.4 million accounts belonged to Australian users; this grew to 2.2 million by October 2015.[[389]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-auscourt1-391)

Valve also considers [concurrent users](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concurrent_user "Concurrent user") – how many accounts were logged in at the same time – a key indicator of the success of the platform. By August 2017, Valve reported that they saw a peak of 14 million concurrent players, up from 8.4 million in 2015, with 33 million active daily and 67 million active monthly.[[388]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-geekwire_aug2017-390) By January 2018, the peak online count had reached 18.5 million, with over 47 million [daily active users](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daily_active_user "Daily active user").[[390]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-392)[[391]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-393) During the [COVID-19 pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic "COVID-19 pandemic") in 2020, in which a large proportion of the world's population were [at home](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_lockdowns "COVID-19 lockdowns"), Steam saw a concurrent player count of over 23 million in March, along with several games seeing similar record-breaking concurrent counts.[[392]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-394) The highest concurrent player count reached 39.2 million by December 2024, in part from the combined releases of _[Marvel Rivals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvel\_Rivals "Marvel Rivals")_ and _[Path of Exile 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Path\_of\_Exile\_2 "Path of Exile 2")_, and 40 million by February 2025 with the release of _[Monster Hunter Wilds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monster\_Hunter\_Wilds "Monster Hunter Wilds")_.[[393]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-395)[[394]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-396)

In October 2025, Steam reached a new all-time concurrent user peak of 41.6 million surpassing its previous record by over a million - a surge attributed largely to the release of [Battlefield 6](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battlefield_6 "Battlefield 6").[[395]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-397) An analysis by Alinea Analytics estimated that in the first 11 months of 2025, Steam had brought in $16.3 billion in revenue.[[396]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-398)

### Sales and distribution

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Sales and distribution")]

[![Image 11](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a9/Garrys-Mod-sales-graph.png/500px-Garrys-Mod-sales-graph.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Garrys-Mod-sales-graph.png)

Sales graph for _[Garry's Mod](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garry%27s\_Mod "Garry's Mod")_, released by the game's developer. The largest spikes are caused by sales and promotions.[[397]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-pcgamer.com-399) By April 2014, it had sold nearly five million copies through the service.[[398]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-400)

The number of new games, by year, published on Steam, estimated by [Steam Spy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_Spy "Steam Spy") in January 2020.[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-sales_by_year-401)[[400]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-pcgi.biz_27k-402)[[401]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-pcgi.biz_34k-403) The years 2004 and 2005 are not visible on this chart.

Steam has grown from seven games in 2004 to over 30,000 by 2019, with additional non-gaming products, such as creation software, DLC, and videos, numbering over 20,000.[[402]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-404) More than 50,000 games were on the service as of February 2021.[[403]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-405) The growth of games on Steam is attributed to changes in Valve's curation approach, which allows publishers to add games without Valve's direct involvement, and games supporting virtual reality technology.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-polygon_steam_growth-202) The addition of Greenlight and Direct has accelerated the number of games present on the service, with almost 40% of the 19,000 games on Steam by the end of 2017 having been released in 2017.[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-sales_by_year-401) Before Greenlight, Valve saw about five new games published each week. Greenlight expanded this to about seventy, and which doubled to one hundred and eighty per week following the introduction of Direct.[[404]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-406)

Although Steam provides direct sales data to developers and publishers, it does not provide public sales data. In 2011, Valve's Jason Holtman stated that the company felt that such data was outdated for a digital market.[[405]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-407)[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-408) Data that Valve does provide cannot be released without permission because of a [non-disclosure agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-disclosure_agreement "Non-disclosure agreement").[[407]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-409)[[408]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-410)

Developers and publishers have asked for some metrics of sales for games, to allow them to judge the potential success of a title by reviewing how similar games have performed. Algorithms that worked on publicly available data through user profiles to estimate sales data with some accuracy led to the creation of the website [Steam Spy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_Spy "Steam Spy") in 2015.[[409]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-411) Steam Spy was credited with being reasonably accurate, but in April 2018, Valve added new privacy settings that defaulted to hiding user game profiles, stating this was part of compliance with the [General Data Protection Regulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Data_Protection_Regulation "General Data Protection Regulation") (GDPR) of the [European Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union "European Union"). The change broke the method by which Steam Spy had collected data, rendering it unusable.[[410]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-412) A few months later, another method had been developed using game achievements to estimate sales with similar accuracy, but Valve shortly changed the Steam API that reduced its functionality. Some have asserted that Valve used the GDPR change as a means to block methods of estimating sales,[[411]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-413) although Valve subsequently promised to provide tools to developers to help gain such insights that they say will be more accurate.[[412]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-414) In 2020, [Simon Carless](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_Carless "Simon Carless") revised an approach originally proposed by [Mike Boxleiter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Boxleiter "Mike Boxleiter") as early as 2013, with Carless's method used to estimate sales based on the number of reviews it has on Steam based on a modified "Boxleiter number" used as a multiplication factor.[[413]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-415)

### Competition and curation impact

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Competition and curation impact")]

The accessibility of publishing games on digital storefronts like Steam has been described as key to the popularity of [indie games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indie_game "Indie game").[[414]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-416) As these processes allow developers to publish games on Steam with minimal oversight from Valve, journalists have criticized Valve for lacking curation policies that make it difficult to find quality games among poorly produced games, sometimes called "shovelware".[[415]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-417)[[416]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-418)

Following the launch of Steam Direct, the video game industry was split on Valve's hands-off approach. Some praised Valve for favoring avoiding trying to be a moral adjudicator of content and letting consumers decide what content they want to see, while others felt that this would encourage developers to publish games that are purposely hateful, and that Valve's reliance on user-filters and algorithms may not succeed in blocking undesirable content. Some further criticized the decision based on the financial gain from avoiding blocking any game content, as Valve collects a cut from sales through Steam.[[417]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-419)[[418]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-420)[[419]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-421)[[420]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-422) In 2018 the [National Center on Sexual Exploitation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Center_on_Sexual_Exploitation "National Center on Sexual Exploitation") denounced the policy for avoiding corporate and social responsibility "in light of the rise of sexual violence and exploitation games being hosted on Steam".[[421]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-423)

Steam was estimated to have the largest share of the PC [digital distribution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_distribution_in_video_games "Digital distribution in video games") market in the 2010s.[[422]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-424)[[423]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-425) In 2013, sales via the Steam catalog are estimated to be between 50 and 75 percent of the total PC gaming market.[[424]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-Graft-426)[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-bloomberg_2013-2) In 2010 and 2013, with an increase in retail copies of major [game publishers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_game_publisher "Video game publisher") integrating or requiring Steam, retailers and journalists referred to the service as a [monopoly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monopoly "Monopoly"), which they claimed can be detrimental to the industry and that sector competition would yield positive results for consumers.[[425]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-427)[[426]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-428) Several developers also noted that Steam's influence on the PC gaming market is powerful and one that smaller developers cannot afford to ignore or not work with, but believe that Valve's corporate practices make it a type of "benevolent dictator".[[427]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-429)

Because of Valve's oversight of sales data, estimates of the market share that Steam has of the videogame market are difficult to compile. [Stardock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stardock "Stardock"), developer of competing platform [Impulse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impulse_(content_delivery) "Impulse (content delivery)"), estimated that Steam had a 70% share in 2009.[[424]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-Graft-426) In February 2011, _[Forbes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forbes "Forbes")_ reported that Steam sales constituted 50–70% of the US$4 billion market for downloaded PC games and that Steam offered game producers [gross margins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_margin "Gross margin") of 70% of the purchase price, compared with 30% at retail.[[428]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-forbes-gnprofile-430)

Steam has been criticized for its reported 30% cut on revenue with publishers from game sales, a value that is similar to other digital storefronts according to [IGN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IGN "IGN").[[429]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-431) However, some critics have asserted that the share no longer scales with cheaper costs of serving data. A 2019 [Game Developers Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game_Developers_Conference "Game Developers Conference") survey showed only 6% of the 400 respondents deemed the share justified.[[430]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-432) Epic Games' [Tim Sweeney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tim_Sweeney "Tim Sweeney") postulated that Valve could reduce its cut to 8%, given that [content delivery network](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Content_delivery_network "Content delivery network") costs has dropped significantly.[[431]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-433) Other services have promoted their sites having a lower cut, including the [Epic Games Store](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epic_Games_Store "Epic Games Store")[[432]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-434) and [Discord](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discord "Discord").[[433]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-435)

In November 2009, online retailers [Impulse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impulse_(software) "Impulse (software)"), [Direct2Drive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct2Drive "Direct2Drive") and [GamersGate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GamersGate "GamersGate") refused to offer _[Call of Duty: Modern Warfare 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Call\_of\_Duty:\_Modern\_Warfare\_2 "Call of Duty: Modern Warfare 2")_ because it includes mandatory installation of Steamworks.[[434]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-:1-436) Direct2Drive accused Steamworks of being a "trojan horse".[[435]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-437) Valve's business development director Jason Holtman replied Steamworks' features were chosen by developers and based on consumer wants and that _Modern Warfare 2_ was one of Steam's "greatest sellers".[[436]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-438) In December 2010, [MCV/Develop](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MCV/Develop "MCV/Develop") reported that "key [traditional](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brick_and_mortar "Brick and mortar") retailers" would stop offering games that integrate Steam.[[437]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-:3-439)

A 2025 report by Gamalytic found that of the approximately 13,000 games released on Steam from January to October 2025, only 8% were estimated to have made revenues over $100,000, while 40% had failed to make more than $100, a cost of applying to publish a game on Steam.[[438]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-440)

### Legal disputes

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steam_(service)&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Legal disputes")]

Steam's predominance has led to Valve becoming involved in various legal cases. The lack of a formal refund policy led the [Australian Competition and Consumer Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australian_Competition_and_Consumer_Commission "Australian Competition and Consumer Commission") (ACCC) to sue Valve in September 2014 for violating Australian consumer laws that required stores to offer refunds for faulty or broken products.[[439]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-441) The ACCC won the lawsuit in March 2016, though recognizing Valve changed its policy in the interim.[[440]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-442) In December 2016, the court fined Valve A$3 million, as well as requiring Valve to include proper language for Australian consumers outlining their rights when purchasing games off of Steam.[[441]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-443) In January 2018, Valve filed for special leave to appeal the decision to the [High Court of Australia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_Court_of_Australia "High Court of Australia"),[[442]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-444) but the High Court dismissed this request.[[443]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-445) In September 2018, Valve's Steam refund policy was found to violate France's consumer laws, and it was fined €147,000 and required to modify its refund policy.[[444]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-446)

In December 2015, the French consumer group [UFC-Que Choisir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UFC-Que_Choisir "UFC-Que Choisir") initiated a lawsuit against Valve for several of its Steam policies that conflicted with French law, including the restriction on [reselling of purchased games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First-sale_doctrine#Application_to_digital_copies "First-sale doctrine"), which is legal within the European Union.[[445]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-447) In September 2019, the [Tribunal de grande instance de Paris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribunal_de_grande_instance_de_Paris "Tribunal de grande instance de Paris") found that Valve's practice of preventing resales violated the EU's [Information Society Directive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_Society_Directive "Information Society Directive") of 2001 and the [Computer Programs Directive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_Programs_Directive "Computer Programs Directive") of 2009, and required them to allow it in the future.[[446]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-448)[[447]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-449) The Interactive Software Federation of Europe (ISFE) issued a statement that the French court ruling goes against established EU case law related to digital copies and threatened to upend much of the digital distribution systems in Europe should it be upheld.[[448]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-450)

In August 2016, [BT Group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BT_Group "BT Group") filed a lawsuit against Valve, stating that Steam's client infringed on four of its patents, which it said were used within Steam's Library, Chat, Messaging, and Broadcasting services.[[449]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-451)[_[needs update](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual\_of\_Style/Dates\_and\_numbers#Chronological\_items "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers")_]

In 2017, the [European Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Commission "European Commission") began investigating Valve and five other publishers—[Bandai Namco Entertainment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bandai_Namco_Entertainment "Bandai Namco Entertainment"), [Capcom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capcom "Capcom"), [Focus Home Interactive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Focus_Home_Interactive "Focus Home Interactive"), [Koch Media](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koch_Media "Koch Media"), and [ZeniMax Media](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ZeniMax_Media "ZeniMax Media")—for anti-competitive practices, specifically the use of [geo-blocking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geo-blocking "Geo-blocking") to prevent access to software within certain countries within the European Economic Area. Such practices would be against the [Digital Single Market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_Single_Market "Digital Single Market") initiative set by the European Union.[[450]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-452) The French gaming trade group, Syndicat National du Jeu Vidéo, noted that geo-blocking was a necessary feature to hinder inappropriate [product key](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Product_key "Product key") reselling.[[451]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-453) The Commission found, in January 2021, that Valve and co-defendants had violated [antitrust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antitrust "Antitrust") rules of the European Union, issued combined fines of €7.8 million, and determined that these companies may be further liable to lawsuits from affected consumers.[[452]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-454) Valve had chosen "not to cooperate", and was fined €1.6 million, the most of any of the defendants.[[453]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-455)

A January 2021 class-action lawsuit filed against Valve asserted that it forced developers into entering a "[most favored nation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Most_favored_nation "Most favored nation")"-type of pricing contract to offer games on their storefront, which required the developers to price their games the same on other platforms as they did on Steam, thus stifling competition.[[454]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-456)_Gamasutra_'s Simon Carless analyzed the lawsuit and observed that Valve's terms only apply the resale of Steam keys and not games themselves, and thus the lawsuit may be without merit.[[455]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-457)

A separate class-action lawsuit filed against Valve by [Wolfire Games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolfire_Games "Wolfire Games") in April 2021 asserted that Steam is essentially a monopoly, since developers must sell to PC users through it and that its 30% cut and "most favored nation" pricing practices violate antitrust laws as a result of their position.[[456]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-458) Valve's response, filed in July 2021, dismissed the complaint stating that it "has no duty under antitrust law to allow developers to use free Steam Keys to undersell prices for the games they sell on Steam—or to provide Steam Keys at all". Valve defended its 30% revenue as meeting the current [Industry standard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technical_standard "Technical standard") and claimed Wolfire's figure for Steam's market share to lack evidence.[[457]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-pcgamer_valve_wolfire_response-459) Wolfire's suit was dismissed by the presiding judge in November 2021 after determining that Wolfire had failed to show that Valve had a monopoly on game sales and that the 30% cut has remained unchanged throughout Valve's history.[[458]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-460) Wolfire refiled its case, narrowing the complaint to Valve's use of its dominance to intimidate developers that sell their game for less on other marketplaces, which the judge allowed to proceed in May 2022.[[459]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-461) According to discovery, Valve was ordered to have Gabe Newell submit to a deposition for discussion of Valve's business strategy related to Steam.[[460]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-462) On November 26, 2024, an order was entered certifying a class of game sellers who were allegedly injured by Valve's policies, and the case is now expected to proceed to trial.[[461]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-20241128PCG-463)

Valve changed the Steam terms of service in September 2024 to eliminate the forced [arbitration clause](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arbitration_clause "Arbitration clause"), such that any disputes with the storefront are to be resolved within courtrooms, and allowing for class-action lawsuits.[[462]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service)#cite_note-464)
